## MANDATORY: Use Sourcegraph Code Search Tools BEFORE Any Code Changes

You have Sourcegraph MCP tools available (keyword_search, nls_search, list_files, read_file, go_to_definition, find_references, deepsearch, deepsearch_read). You MUST use them as your primary code discovery method.

Use `list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.

**CRITICAL — TWO-PHASE WORKFLOW:**

### Phase 1: Search & Understand (MANDATORY — DO NOT SKIP)
BEFORE writing ANY code, modifying ANY file, or running ANY implementation command, you MUST:
1. Read the task instructions and identify key functions, classes, files, or concepts mentioned
2. Make at least 3 Sourcegraph search calls to find and understand the relevant code:
   - Use `keyword_search` with the repo filter to find specific symbols/identifiers from the task
   - Use `list_files` to understand the project structure
   - Use `go_to_definition` / `find_references` to trace code relationships
3. DO NOT start implementing until you have searched for the key terms from the task
5. Use `deepsearch` for dependency/impact analysis — understand blast radius of changes, find callers of modified functions, downstream consumers of changed interfaces, and tests covering affected code paths
6. `deepsearch` returns a polling link, NOT immediate results. After calling it, continue working with other tools for 30-60 seconds, then call `deepsearch_read` with the polling link
7. Retry `deepsearch_read` at least 3 times — Deep Search takes 50-120 seconds to complete
8. For code review tasks: the PR diff alone does NOT show full impact. Use `deepsearch` to find what else depends on the changed code before finalizing your review

### Phase 2: Implement
After understanding the codebase through Sourcegraph:
1. Use Read to verify local file contents (Sourcegraph indexes latest branch, local may differ)
2. If Sourcegraph shows different code than local, TRUST THE LOCAL CODE
3. Make your code changes — stop searching, focus on implementation

See CLAUDE.md for the complete tool selection guide.

# Task: Document Cilium eBPF Map API

## Objective

Generate comprehensive API reference documentation for Cilium's eBPF map API in the `pkg/bpf` package. The documentation should serve as a complete reference for developers working with eBPF maps in Cilium.

## Scope

Focus on the Go wrappers in `pkg/bpf` that provide user-space interaction with kernel eBPF maps. Document:

1. **Core Map Type and Creation**
   - `Map` struct and its primary methods
   - Map creation functions (`NewMap`, `OpenMap`, `OpenOrCreate`)
   - Map lifecycle operations (Open, Create, Close, Recreate)

2. **CRUD Operations**
   - Lookup, Update, Delete operations
   - Batch operations (BatchLookup, DeleteAll)
   - Per-CPU map operations
   - Locked operations (DeleteLocked)

3. **Iteration and Dumping**
   - Dump methods and callbacks
   - BatchIterator type and usage
   - DumpStats for tracking iteration

4. **Pinning and Persistence**
   - Pin/Unpin operations
   - BPF filesystem paths (BPFFSRoot, CiliumPath, MapPath)
   - Map persistence behavior

5. **Key/Value Interfaces**
   - MapKey, MapValue, MapPerCPUValue interfaces
   - EndpointKey as concrete example

6. **Event System**
   - Event types (MapUpdate, MapDelete)
   - DumpAndSubscribe for event streaming
   - Event callbacks and handles

7. **Collection Loading**
   - LoadCollection and LoadAndAssign functions
   - CollectionOptions

## Requirements

Your documentation must include:

1. **API Method Signatures**: Complete signatures with parameter types and return values
2. **Behavioral Semantics**:
   - When maps are pinned vs unpinned
   - Difference between Create() and CreateUnpinned()
   - OpenOrCreate() behavior on existing maps
   - How deletion works within DumpCallback (requires DeleteLocked)
   - Event subscription lifecycle
   - Batch iterator retry behavior on ENOSPC
3. **Usage Examples**: Code snippets showing:
   - Basic map creation and CRUD
   - Iteration with BatchIterator
   - Event subscription and cleanup
   - Pinning and unpinning maps
   - Real-world patterns from Cilium internals
4. **Documentation Structure**: Organize clearly with sections for each category above

## Deliverable

Write your documentation to `/workspace/documentation.md` in Markdown format.

## Constraints

- Do NOT include file paths or specific implementation locations in the documentation
- Focus on API contracts and behavior, not internal implementation details
- Include enough behavioral detail that users can correctly use the API without reading source code
- Provide accurate examples that would compile and work correctly

The documentation has been written to `/workspace/documentation.md`. Here's a summary of what's covered:

1. **Key/Value Interfaces** — `MapKey`, `MapValue`, `MapPerCPUValue`, `KeyValue`, and `StructBinaryMarshaler` with usage examples
2. **Core Map Type and Creation** — `Map` struct, `NewMap`, `NewMapWithInnerSpec`, `OpenMap` with parameter details and behavioral notes
3. **Map Lifecycle Operations** — `OpenOrCreate`, `CreateUnpinned`, `Create`, `Open`, `Close`, `Recreate`, `IsOpen` with behavioral semantics (pinning vs unpinned, spec consumption, etc.)
4. **CRUD Operations** — `Lookup`, `Update`, `Delete`, `SilentDelete`, `DeleteLocked` (with deadlock avoidance explanation), `DeleteAll`, `ClearAll`
5. **Iteration and Dumping** — `DumpWithCallback`, `DumpPerCPUWithCallback`, `DumpReliablyWithCallback` (with lock semantics and `ErrMaxLookup`), `Dump`, `DumpIfExists`
6. **Batch Iterator** — Full generic type signatures, `IterateAll` with ENOSPC retry behavior, options (`WithMaxRetries`, `WithStartingChunkSize`, `WithEBPFBatchOpts`), `CountAll`, `BatchCount`
7. **DumpStats** — All fields and usage with `DumpReliablyWithCallback`
8. **Pinning and Persistence** — `BPFFSRoot`, `CiliumPath`, `MapPath`, `Pin`/`Unpin` operations, pinning behavior comparison table
9. **Event System** — `WithEvents`, `Event` type, `DumpAndSubscribe`, `Handle` with backpressure semantics, lifecycle management, usage example
10. **Collection Loading** — `LoadCollectionSpec` (with tail call analysis), `LoadCollection` (with deferred commit pattern), `LoadAndAssign`, `CollectionOptions`
11. **EndpointKey** — Concrete `MapKey` example
12. **Map Memory Flags** — Pre-allocation and distributed LRU settings
13. **Builder Pattern** — `WithCache`, `WithEvents`, `WithPressureMetric`, `WithGroupName`

It is identical to Open() but should be used when\\n643: // m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\\n644: // writing.\\n645: func (m *Map) open() error {\\n646: \\tif m.m != nil {\\n647: \\t\\treturn nil\\n648: \\t}\\n649: \\n650: \\tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\\n651: \\t\\treturn err\\n652: \\t}\\n653: \\n654: \\tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\\n655: \\tif err != nil {\\n656: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"loading pinned map %s: %w\\\", m.path, err)\\n657: \\t}\\n658: \\n659: \\tm.updateMetrics()\\n660: \\tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\\n661: \\n662: \\tm.m = em\\n663: \\n664: \\treturn nil\\n665: }\\n666: \\n667: func (m *Map) Close() error {\\n668: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n669: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n670: \\n671: \\tif m.enableSync {\\n672: \\t\\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\\n673: \\t}\\n674: \\n675: \\tif m.m != nil {\\n676: \\t\\tm.m.Close()\\n677: \\t\\tm.m = nil\\n678: \\t}\\n679: \\n680: \\tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\\n681: \\n682: \\treturn nil\\n683: }\\n684: \\n685: func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\\n686: \\tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\\n687: \\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\\n688: \\t\\tduration = spanstat.Start()\\n689: \\t}\\n690: \\n691: \\terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\\n692: \\n693: \\tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\\n694: \\t\\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\\n695: \\t}\\n696: \\n697: \\treturn err\\n698: }\\n699: \\n700: type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\\n701: \\n702: // DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\\n703: // each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n705: //\\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n708: \\tif cb == nil {\\n709: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n710: \\t}\\n711: \\n712: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n713: \\t\\treturn err\\n714: \\t}\\n715: \\n716: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n717: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n718: \\n719: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n720: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n721: \\tmv := m.value.New()\\n722: \\n723: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n724: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n725: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n726: \\n727: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n728: \\t\\tmv = m.value.New()\\n729: \\t}\\n730: \\n731: \\treturn i.Err()\\n732: }\\n733: \\n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\\n737: \\n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\\n743: \\tif cb == nil {\\n744: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n745: \\t}\\n746: \\n747: \\tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\\n748: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\\\", m.name)\\n749: \\t}\\n750: \\n751: \\tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\\n752: \\tif !ok {\\n753: \\t\\treturn fmt.Errorf(\\\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\\\", m.name)\\n754: \\t}\\n755: \\n756: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n757: \\t\\treturn err\\n758: \\t}\\n759: \\n760: \\tm.lock.RLock()\\n761: \\tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\\n762: \\n763: \\t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\\n764: \\tmk := m.key.New()\\n765: \\tmv := v.NewSlice()\\n766: \\n767: \\ti := m.m.Iterate()\\n768: \\tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\\n769: \\t\\tcb(mk, mv)\\n770: \\n771: \\t\\tmk = m.key.New()\\n772: \\t\\tmv = v.NewSlice()\\n773: \\t}\\n774: \\n775: \\treturn i.Err()\\n776: }\\n777: \\n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\\n781: \\tfound, err := m.exist()\\n782: \\tif err != nil {\\n783: \\t\\treturn err\\n784: \\t}\\n785: \\n786: \\tif found {\\n787: \\t\\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\\n788: \\t}\\n789: \\n790: \\treturn nil\\n791: }\\n792: \\n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\\n799: //\\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\\n804: \\tif cb == nil {\\n805: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"empty callback\\\")\\n806: \\t}\\n807: \\n808: \\tif stats == nil {\\n809: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"stats is nil\\\")\\n810: \\t}\\n811: \\n812: \\tvar (\\n813: \\t\\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\\n814: \\t\\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\\n815: \\t\\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\\n816: \\t\\tvalue      = m.value.New()\\n817: \\n818: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n819: \\t)\\n820: \\n821: \\tstats.start()\\n822: \\tdefer stats.finish()\\n823: \\n824: \\tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\\n825: \\t\\treturn err\\n826: \\t}\\n827: \\n828: \\t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\\n829: \\t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\\n830: \\t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\\n831: \\tm.lock.Lock()\\n832: \\tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\\n833: \\tif m.m == nil {\\n834: \\t\\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\\n835: \\t\\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\\n836: \\t\\treturn errors.New(\\\"map is closed\\\")\\n837: \\t}\\n838: \\n839: \\t// Get the first map key.\\n840: \\tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\\n841: \\t\\tstats.Lookup = 1\\n842: \\t\\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n843: \\t\\t\\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\\n844: \\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n845: \\t\\t\\treturn nil\\n846: \\t\\t}\\n847: \\t}\\n848: \\n849: \\t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\\n850: \\t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\\n851: \\t// updated while being iterated)\\n852: \\tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\\n853: \\n854: \\t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\\n855: \\t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\\n856: \\t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\\n857: \\tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\\n858: \\t\\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\\n859: \\t\\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\\n860: \\t\\t//\\n861: \\t\\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\\n862: \\t\\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\\n863: \\t\\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\\n864: \\t\\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\\n865: \\t\\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\\n866: \\n867: \\t\\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\\n868: \\t\\t\\tstats.LookupFailed++\\n869: \\t\\t\\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\\n870: \\t\\t\\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\\n871: \\t\\t\\tif prevKeyValid {\\n872: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = prevKey\\n873: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\\n874: \\t\\t\\t\\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\\n875: \\t\\t\\t\\tprevKeyValid = false\\n876: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.KeyFallback++\\n877: \\t\\t\\t} else {\\n878: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\\n879: \\t\\t\\t\\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\\n880: \\t\\t\\t\\t// one, or the first element in the map.\\n881: \\t\\t\\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n882: \\t\\t\\t\\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\\n883: \\t\\t\\t\\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\\n884: \\t\\t\\t\\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\\n885: \\t\\t\\t\\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n887: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Interrupted++\\n888: \\t\\t\\t}\\n889: \\t\\t\\tcontinue\\n890: \\t\\t}\\n891: \\n892: \\t\\tcb(currentKey, value)\\n893: \\n894: \\t\\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\\n895: \\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\\n896: \\t\\t\\t\\tstats.Completed = true\\n897: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\\n898: \\t\\t\\t}\\n899: \\t\\t\\treturn nextKeyErr\\n900: \\t\\t}\\n901: \\n902: \\t\\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\\n903: \\t\\tprevKey = currentKey\\n904: \\t\\tcurrentKey = nextKey\\n905: \\t\\tnextKey = m.key.New()\\n906: \\t\\tprevKeyValid = true\\n907: \\t}\\n908: \\n909: \\treturn ErrMaxLookup\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\\n913: // of bpf maps.\\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\\n915: \\tm    *Map\\n916: \\terr  error\\n917: \\tkeys []KT\\n918: \\tvals []VT\\n919: \\n920: \\tchunkSize      int\\n921: \\tmaxDumpRetries uint32\\n922: \\n923: \\t// Iteration stats\\n924: \\tbatchSize int\\n925: \\n926: \\topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\\n927: }\\n928: \\n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\\n951: //\\t\\t// ...\\n952: //\\t}\\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, \\treturn kvs.err\\n979: }\\n980: \\n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\\n982: \\tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\\n983: \\t\\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\\n984: \\t}\\n985: \\treturn defaultBatchedRetries\\n986: }\\n987: \\n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\\n989: \\n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\\n991: \\n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1011: \\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1012: \\t\\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\\n1013: \\t\\treturn in\\n1014: \\t}\\n1015: }\\n1016: \\n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1020: \\treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\\n1021: \\t\\tin.chunkSize = size\\n1022: \\t\\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\\n1023: \\t\\t\\tin.chunkSize = 8\\n1024: \\t\\t}\\n1025: \\t\\treturn in\\n1026: \\t}\\n1027: }\\n1028: \\n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\\n1030: // iterator.\\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\\n1032: \\tc := 0\\n1033: \\tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\\n1034: \\t\\tc++\\n1035: \\t}\\n1036: \\treturn c, iter.Err()\\n1037: }\\n1038: \\n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\\n1040: \\tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\\n1041: \\tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\\n1042: \\treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\\n1043: }\\n1044: \\n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\\n1046: // using the batched API.\\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\\n1052: //\\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\\n1054: //\\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\\n1057: \\tswitch bi.m.Type() {\\n1058: \\tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\\n1059: \\t\\tbreak\\n1060: \\tdefault:\\n1061: \\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\\\", bi.m.Type())\\n1062: \\t\\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\\n1063: \\t}\\n1064: \\n1065: \\tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\\n1066: \\n1067: \\tfor _, opt := range opts {\\n1068: \\t\\tif opt != nil {\\n1069: \\t\\t\\tbi = opt(bi)\\n1070: \\t\\t}\\n1071: \\t}\\n1072: \\n1073: \\t// reset values\\n1074: \\tbi.err = nil\\n1075: \\tbi.batchSize = 0\\n1076: \\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1077: \\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1078: \\n1079: \\tprocessed := 0\\n1080: \\tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\\n1081: \\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\\n1082: \\t\\tif bi.Err() != nil {\\n1083: \\t\\t\\treturn\\n1084: \\t\\t}\\n1085: \\n1086: \\titerate:\\n1087: \\t\\tfor {\\n1088: \\t\\t\\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\\n1089: \\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\\n1090: \\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n1091: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1092: \\t\\tretry:\\n1093: \\t\\t\\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\\n1094: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\\n1095: \\t\\t\\t\\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\\n1096: \\t\\t\\t\\tbi.batchSize = c\\n1097: \\n1098: \\t\\t\\t\\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\\n1099: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\\n1100: \\t\\t\\t\\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\\n1101: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\\n1102: \\t\\t\\t\\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\\n1103: \\t\\t\\t\\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\\n1104: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1105: \\t\\t\\t\\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\\n1106: \\t\\t\\t\\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\\n1107: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1108: \\t\\t\\t\\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\\n1109: \\t\\t\\t\\t//\\n1110: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\\n1111: \\t\\t\\t\\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\\n1112: \\t\\t\\t\\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\\n1113: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\\n1114: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = batchErr\\n1115: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t} else {\\n1116: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\\n1117: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1118: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\\n1119: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1120: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tcontinue retry\\n1121: \\t\\t\\t\\t} \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\\\"failed to iterate map: %w\\\", batchErr)\\n1125: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn\\n1126: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1127: \\n1128: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Yield all received pairs.\\n1129: \\t\\t\\t\\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\\n1130: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tprocessed++\\n1131: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\\n1132: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbreak iterate\\n1133: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1134: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1135: \\n1136: \\t\\t\\t\\tif done {\\n1137: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tbreak iterate\\n1138: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n1139: \\t\\t\\t\\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\\n1140: \\t\\t\\t}\\n1141: \\t\\t}\\n1142: \\t}\\n1143: }\\n1144: \\n1145: // Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\\n1146: // data stored in BPF map.\\n1147: func It is identical to Open() but should be used when\n643: // m.lock is already held. open() may only be used if m.lock is held for\n644: // writing.\n645: func (m *Map) open() error {\n646: \tif m.m != nil {\n647: \t\treturn nil\n648: \t}\n649: \n650: \tif err := m.setPathIfUnset(); err != nil {\n651: \t\treturn err\n652: \t}\n653: \n654: \tem, err := ebpf.LoadPinnedMap(m.path, nil)\n655: \tif err != nil {\n656: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"loading pinned map %s: %w\", m.path, err)\n657: \t}\n658: \n659: \tm.updateMetrics()\n660: \tregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n661: \n662: \tm.m = em\n663: \n664: \treturn nil\n665: }\n666: \n667: func (m *Map) Close() error {\n668: \tm.lock.Lock()\n669: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n670: \n671: \tif m.enableSync {\n672: \t\tmapControllers.RemoveController(m.controllerName())\n673: \t}\n674: \n675: \tif m.m != nil {\n676: \t\tm.m.Close()\n677: \t\tm.m = nil\n678: \t}\n679: \n680: \tunregisterMap(m.Logger, m.path, m)\n681: \n682: \treturn nil\n683: }\n684: \n685: func (m *Map) NextKey(key, nextKeyOut any) error {\n686: \tvar duration *spanstat.SpanStat\n687: \tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n688: \t\tduration = spanstat.Start()\n689: \t}\n690: \n691: \terr := m.m.NextKey(key, nextKeyOut)\n692: \n693: \tif metrics.BPFSyscallDuration.IsEnabled() {\n694: \t\tmetrics.BPFSyscallDuration.WithLabelValues(metricOpGetNextKey, metrics.Error2Outcome(err)).Observe(duration.End(err == nil).Total().Seconds())\n695: \t}\n696: \n697: \treturn err\n698: }\n699: \n700: type DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n701: \n702: // DumpWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given DumpCallback for\n703: // each map entry. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks to\n704: // retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n705: //\n706: // To dump per-cpu maps, use DumpPerCPUWithCallback.\n707: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error {\n708: \tif cb == nil {\n709: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n710: \t}\n711: \n712: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n713: \t\treturn err\n714: \t}\n715: \n716: \tm.lock.RLock()\n717: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n718: \n719: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n720: \tmk := m.key.New()\n721: \tmv := m.value.New()\n722: \n723: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n724: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n725: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n726: \n727: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n728: \t\tmv = m.value.New()\n729: \t}\n730: \n731: \treturn i.Err()\n732: }\n733: \n734: // DumpPerCPUCallback is called by DumpPerCPUWithCallback with the map key and\n735: // the slice of all values from all CPUs.\n736: type DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n737: \n738: // DumpPerCPUWithCallback iterates over the Map and calls the given\n739: // DumpPerCPUCallback for each map entry, passing the slice with all values\n740: // from all CPUs. With the current implementation, it is safe for callbacks\n741: // to retain the values received, as they are guaranteed to be new instances.\n742: func (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error {\n743: \tif cb == nil {\n744: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n745: \t}\n746: \n747: \tif !m.hasPerCPUValue() {\n748: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s is not a per-CPU map\", m.name)\n749: \t}\n750: \n751: \tv, ok := m.value.(MapPerCPUValue)\n752: \tif !ok {\n753: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"map %s value type does not implement MapPerCPUValue\", m.name)\n754: \t}\n755: \n756: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n757: \t\treturn err\n758: \t}\n759: \n760: \tm.lock.RLock()\n761: \tdefer m.lock.RUnlock()\n762: \n763: \t// Don't need deep copies here, only fresh pointers.\n764: \tmk := m.key.New()\n765: \tmv := v.NewSlice()\n766: \n767: \ti := m.m.Iterate()\n768: \tfor i.Next(mk, mv) {\n769: \t\tcb(mk, mv)\n770: \n771: \t\tmk = m.key.New()\n772: \t\tmv = v.NewSlice()\n773: \t}\n774: \n775: \treturn i.Err()\n776: }\n777: \n778: // DumpWithCallbackIfExists is similar to DumpWithCallback, but returns earlier\n779: // if the given map does not exist.\n780: func (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error {\n781: \tfound, err := m.exist()\n782: \tif err != nil {\n783: \t\treturn err\n784: \t}\n785: \n786: \tif found {\n787: \t\treturn m.DumpWithCallback(cb)\n788: \t}\n789: \n790: \treturn nil\n791: }\n792: \n793: // DumpReliablyWithCallback is similar to DumpWithCallback, but performs\n794: // additional tracking of the current and recently seen keys, so that if an\n795: // element is removed from the underlying kernel map during the dump, the dump\n796: // can continue from a recently seen key rather than restarting from scratch.\n797: // In addition, it caps the maximum number of map entry iterations at 4 times\n798: // the maximum map size. If this limit is reached, ErrMaxLookup is returned.\n799: //\n800: // The caller must provide a callback for handling each entry, and a stats\n801: // object initialized via a call to NewDumpStats(). The callback function must\n802: // not invoke any map operations that acquire the Map.lock.\n803: func (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error {\n804: \tif cb == nil {\n805: \t\treturn errors.New(\"empty callback\")\n806: \t}\n807: \n808: \tif stats == nil {\n809: \t\treturn errors.New(\"stats is nil\")\n810: \t}\n811: \n812: \tvar (\n813: \t\tprevKey    = m.key.New()\n814: \t\tcurrentKey = m.key.New()\n815: \t\tnextKey    = m.key.New()\n816: \t\tvalue      = m.value.New()\n817: \n818: \t\tprevKeyValid = false\n819: \t)\n820: \n821: \tstats.start()\n822: \tdefer stats.finish()\n823: \n824: \tif err := m.Open(); err != nil {\n825: \t\treturn err\n826: \t}\n827: \n828: \t// Acquire a (write) lock here as callers can invoke map operations in the\n829: \t// DumpCallback that need a (write) lock.\n830: \t// See PR for more details. - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/pull/38590.\n831: \tm.lock.Lock()\n832: \tdefer m.lock.Unlock()\n833: \tif m.m == nil {\n834: \t\t// We currently don't prevent open maps from being closed.\n835: \t\t// See GH issue - https://github.com/cilium/cilium/issues/39287.\n836: \t\treturn errors.New(\"map is closed\")\n837: \t}\n838: \n839: \t// Get the first map key.\n840: \tif err := m.NextKey(nil, currentKey); err != nil {\n841: \t\tstats.Lookup = 1\n842: \t\tif errors.Is(err, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n843: \t\t\t// Empty map, nothing to iterate.\n844: \t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n845: \t\t\treturn nil\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \t// maxLookup is an upper bound limit to prevent backtracking forever\n850: \t// when iterating over the map's elements (the map might be concurrently\n851: \t// updated while being iterated)\n852: \tmaxLookup := stats.MaxEntries * 4\n853: \n854: \t// This loop stops when all elements have been iterated (Map.NextKey() returns\n855: \t// ErrKeyNotExist) OR, in order to avoid hanging if\n856: \t// the map is continuously updated, when maxLookup has been reached\n857: \tfor stats.Lookup = 1; stats.Lookup <= maxLookup; stats.Lookup++ {\n858: \t\t// currentKey was set by the first m.NextKey() above. We know it existed in\n859: \t\t// the map, but it may have been deleted by a concurrent map operation.\n860: \t\t//\n861: \t\t// If currentKey is no longer in the map, nextKey may be the first key in\n862: \t\t// the map again. Continue with nextKey only if we still find currentKey in\n863: \t\t// the Lookup() after the call to m.NextKey(), this way we know nextKey is\n864: \t\t// NOT the first key in the map and iteration hasn't reset.\n865: \t\tnextKeyErr := m.NextKey(currentKey, nextKey)\n866: \n867: \t\tif err := m.m.Lookup(currentKey, value); err != nil {\n868: \t\t\tstats.LookupFailed++\n869: \t\t\t// Restarting from a invalid key starts the iteration again from the beginning.\n870: \t\t\t// If we have a previously found key, try to restart from there instead\n871: \t\t\tif prevKeyValid {\n872: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = prevKey\n873: \t\t\t\t// Restart from a given previous key only once, otherwise if the prevKey is\n874: \t\t\t\t// concurrently deleted we might loop forever trying to look it up.\n875: \t\t\t\tprevKeyValid = false\n876: \t\t\t\tstats.KeyFallback++\n877: \t\t\t} else {\n878: \t\t\t\t// Depending on exactly when currentKey was deleted from the\n879: \t\t\t\t// map, nextKey may be the actual key element after the deleted\n880: \t\t\t\t// one, or the first element in the map.\n881: \t\t\t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n882: \t\t\t\t// To avoid having nextKey and currentKey pointing at the same memory\n883: \t\t\t\t// we allocate a new key for nextKey. Without this currentKey and nextKey\n884: \t\t\t\t// would be the same pointer value and would get double iterated on the next\n885: \t\t\t\t// iterations m.NextKey(...) call.\n886: \t\t\t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n887: \t\t\t\tstats.Interrupted++\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t\tcontinue\n890: \t\t}\n891: \n892: \t\tcb(currentKey, value)\n893: \n894: \t\tif nextKeyErr != nil {\n895: \t\t\tif errors.Is(nextKeyErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist) {\n896: \t\t\t\tstats.Completed = true\n897: \t\t\t\treturn nil // end of map, we're done iterating\n898: \t\t\t}\n899: \t\t\treturn nextKeyErr\n900: \t\t}\n901: \n902: \t\t// Prepare keys to move to the next iteration.\n903: \t\tprevKey = currentKey\n904: \t\tcurrentKey = nextKey\n905: \t\tnextKey = m.key.New()\n906: \t\tprevKeyValid = true\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn ErrMaxLookup\n910: }\n911: \n912: // BatchIterator provides a typed wrapper *Map that allows for batched iteration\n913: // of bpf maps.\n914: type BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n915: \tm    *Map\n916: \terr  error\n917: \tkeys []KT\n918: \tvals []VT\n919: \n920: \tchunkSize      int\n921: \tmaxDumpRetries uint32\n922: \n923: \t// Iteration stats\n924: \tbatchSize int\n925: \n926: \topts *ebpf.BatchOptions\n927: }\n928: \n929: // NewBatchIterator that allows for iterating a map using the bpf batch api.\n930: // This automatically handles concerns such as batch sizing and handling errors\n931: // when end of map is reached.\n932: // Following iteration, any unresolved errors encountered when iterating\n933: // the bpf map can be accessed via the Err() function.\n934: // The pointer type of KT & VT must implement Map{Key,Value}, respectively.\n935: //\n936: // Subsequent iterations via IterateAll reset all internal state and begin\n937: // iteration over.\n938: //\n939: // Example usage:\n940: //\n941: //\tm := NewMap(\"cilium_test\",\n942: //\t\tebpf.Hash,\n943: //\t\t&TestKey{}, \t// *TestKey implements MapKey.\n944: //\t\t&TestValue{}, \t// *TestValue implements MapValue.\n945: //\t\tmapSize,\n946: //\t\tBPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n947: //\t)\n948: //\n949: //\titer := NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\n950: //\tfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n951: //\t\t// ...\n952: //\t}\n953: func NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n954: \treturn &BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]{\n955: \t\tm: m,\n956: \t}\n957: }\n958: \n959: // KeyPointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n960: // of a type T is a MapKey.\n961: type KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n962: \tMapKey\n963: \t*T\n964: }\n965: \n966: // ValuePointer is a generic interface that provides the constraint that the pointer\n967: // of a type T is a MapValue.\n968: type ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n969: \tMapValue\n970: \t*T\n971: }\n972: \n973: // Err returns errors encountered during the previous iteration when\n974: // IterateAll(...) is called.\n975: //\n976: // If the iterator is reused, the error will be reset,\n977: func (kvs BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error {\n978: \treturn kvs.err\n979: }\n980: \n981: func (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) maxBatchedRetries() int {\n982: \tif bi.maxDumpRetries > 0 {\n983: \t\treturn int(bi.maxDumpRetries)\n984: \t}\n985: \treturn defaultBatchedRetries\n986: }\n987: \n988: const defaultBatchedRetries = 3\n989: \n990: type BatchIteratorOpt[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] func(*BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n991: \n992: // WithEBPFBatchOpts returns a batch iterator option that allows for overriding\n993: // BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH options.\n994: func WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n995: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n996: \t\tin.opts = opts\n997: \t\treturn in\n998: \t}\n999: }\n1000: \n1001: // WithMaxRetries returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the default\n1002: // max batch retries.\n1003: //\n1004: // Unless the starting chunk size is set to be the map size, it is possible for iteration\n1005: // to fail with ENOSPC if the passed allocated chunk array size is not big enough to accommodate\n1006: // a the bpf maps underlying hashmaps bucket size.\n1007: //\n1008: // If this happens, BatchIterator will automatically attempt to double the batch size and\n1009: // retry the iteration from the same place - up to a number of retries.\n1010: func WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1011: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1012: \t\tin.maxDumpRetries = retries\n1013: \t\treturn in\n1014: \t}\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: // WithStartingChunkSize returns a batch iterator option that allows overriding the dynamically\n1018: // chosen starting chunk size.\n1019: func WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1020: \treturn func(in *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP] {\n1021: \t\tin.chunkSize = size\n1022: \t\tif in.chunkSize <= 0 {\n1023: \t\t\tin.chunkSize = 8\n1024: \t\t}\n1025: \t\treturn in\n1026: \t}\n1027: }\n1028: \n1029: // CountAll is a helper function that returns the count of all elements in a batched\n1030: // iterator.\n1031: func CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error) {\n1032: \tc := 0\n1033: \tfor range iter.IterateAll(ctx) {\n1034: \t\tc++\n1035: \t}\n1036: \treturn c, iter.Err()\n1037: }\n1038: \n1039: func startingChunkSize(maxEntries int) int {\n1040: \tbucketSize := math.Sqrt(float64(maxEntries * 2))\n1041: \tnearest2 := math.Log2(bucketSize)\n1042: \treturn int(math.Pow(2, math.Ceil(nearest2)))\n1043: }\n1044: \n1045: // IterateAll returns an iterate Seq2 type which can be used to iterate a map\n1046: // using the batched API.\n1047: // In the case of a the iteration failing due to insufficient batch buffer size,\n1048: // this will attempt to grow the buffer by a factor of 2 (up to a default: 3 amount\n1049: // of retries) and re-attempt the iteration.\n1050: // If the number of failures exceeds max retries, then iteration will stop and an error\n1051: // will be returned via Err().\n1052: //\n1053: // All other errors will result in immediate termination of iterator.\n1054: //\n1055: // If the iteration fails, then the Err() function will return the error that caused the failure.\n1056: func (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP] {\n1057: \tswitch bi.m.Type() {\n1058: \tcase ebpf.Hash, ebpf.LRUHash, ebpf.LPMTrie:\n1059: \t\tbreak\n1060: \tdefault:\n1061: \t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"unsupported map type %s, must be one either hash or lru-hash types\", bi.m.Type())\n1062: \t\treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {}\n1063: \t}\n1064: \n1065: \tbi.chunkSize = startingChunkSize(int(bi.m.MaxEntries()))\n1066: \n1067: \tfor _, opt := range opts {\n1068: \t\tif opt != nil {\n1069: \t\t\tbi = opt(bi)\n1070: \t\t}\n1071: \t}\n1072: \n1073: \t// reset values\n1074: \tbi.err = nil\n1075: \tbi.batchSize = 0\n1076: \tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1077: \tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1078: \n1079: \tprocessed := 0\n1080: \tvar cursor ebpf.MapBatchCursor\n1081: \treturn func(yield func(KP, VP) bool) {\n1082: \t\tif bi.Err() != nil {\n1083: \t\t\treturn\n1084: \t\t}\n1085: \n1086: \titerate:\n1087: \t\tfor {\n1088: \t\t\tif ctx.Err() != nil {\n1089: \t\t\t\tbi.err = ctx.Err()\n1090: \t\t\t\treturn\n1091: \t\t\t}\n1092: \t\tretry:\n1093: \t\t\tfor retry := range bi.maxBatchedRetries() {\n1094: \t\t\t\t// Attempt to read batch into buffer.\n1095: \t\t\t\tc, batchErr := bi.m.BatchLookup(&cursor, bi.keys, bi.vals, nil)\n1096: \t\t\t\tbi.batchSize = c\n1097: \n1098: \t\t\t\tdone := errors.Is(batchErr, ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist)\n1099: \t\t\t\t// Lookup batch on LRU hash map may fail if the buffer passed is not big enough to\n1100: \t\t\t\t// accommodate the largest bucket size in the LRU map [1]\n1101: \t\t\t\t// Because bucket size, in general, cannot be known, we approximate a good starting\n1102: \t\t\t\t// buffer size from the approximation of how many entries there should be in the map\n1103: \t\t\t\t// before expect to see a hash map collision: sqrt(max_entries * 2)\n1104: \t\t\t\t//\n1105: \t\t\t\t// If we receive ENOSPC failures, we will try to recover by growing the batch buffer\n1106: \t\t\t\t// size (up to some max number of retries - default: 3) and retrying the iteration.\n1107: \t\t\t\t//\n1108: \t\t\t\t// [1] https://elixir.bootlin.com/linux/v6.12.6/source/kernel/bpf/hashtab.c#L1807-L1809\n1109: \t\t\t\t//\n1110: \t\t\t\t// Note: If this failure happens during the bpf syscall, it is expected that the underlying\n1111: \t\t\t\t// cursor will not have been swapped - meaning that we can retry the iteration at the same cursor.\n1112: \t\t\t\tif errors.Is(batchErr, unix.ENOSPC) {\n1113: \t\t\t\t\tif retry == bi.maxBatchedRetries()-1 {\n1114: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.err = batchErr\n1115: \t\t\t\t\t} else {\n1116: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.chunkSize *= 2\n1117: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.keys = make([]KT, bi.chunkSize)\n1118: \t\t\t\t\t\tbi.vals = make([]VT, bi.chunkSize)\n1119: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1120: \t\t\t\t\tcontinue retry\n1121: \t\t\t\t} else if !done && batchErr != nil {\n1122: \t\t\t\t\t// If we're not done, and we didn't hit a ENOSPC then stop iteration and record\n1123: \t\t\t\t\t// the error.\n1124: \t\t\t\t\tbi.err = fmt.Errorf(\"failed to iterate map: %w\", batchErr)\n1125: \t\t\t\t\treturn\n1126: \t\t\t\t}\n1127: \n1128: \t\t\t\t// Yield all received pairs.\n1129: \t\t\t\tfor i := range bi.batchSize {\n1130: \t\t\t\t\tprocessed++\n1131: \t\t\t\t\tif !yield(&bi.keys[i], &bi.vals[i]) {\n1132: \t\t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1133: \t\t\t\t\t}\n1134: \t\t\t\t}\n1135: \n1136: \t\t\t\tif done {\n1137: \t\t\t\t\tbreak iterate\n1138: \t\t\t\t}\n1139: \t\t\t\tbreak retry // finish retry loop for this batch.\n1140: \t\t\t}\n1141: \t\t}\n1142: \t}\n1143: }\n1144: \n1145: // Dump returns the map (type map[string][]string) which contains all\n1146: // data stored in BPF map.\n1147: func (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error {\n1148: \tcallback := func(key MapKey, value MapValue) {\n1149: \t\t// No need to deep copy since we are creating strings.\n1150: \t\thash[key.String()] = append(hash[key.String()], value.String())\n1151: \t}\n1152: \n1153: \tif err := m.DumpWithCallback(callback); err != nil {\n1154: \t\treturn err\n1155: {
  "content": "# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\nThe `bpf` package provides Go wrappers for interacting with kernel eBPF maps from user space. It offers a high-level API for creating, reading, updating, and deleting map entries, as well as facilities for map pinning, event streaming, batch iteration, and eBPF collection loading.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n2. [Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)\n3. [Map Lifecycle Operations](#map-lifecycle-operations)\n4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n6. [Batch Iterator](#batch-iterator)\n7. [DumpStats](#dumpstats)\n8. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n9. [Event System](#event-system)\n10. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n11. [EndpointKey (Concrete Key Example)](#endpointkey)\n12. [Map Memory Flags](#map-memory-flags)\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\nAll map operations are typed through these interfaces. Any type used as a key or value in a `Map` must implement the corresponding interface.\n\n### MapKey\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapKey of the same\n    // concrete type. Used internally to allocate buffers for iteration\n    // and lookup.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapValue of the same\n    // concrete type.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue\n\nFor per-CPU map types (`PerCPUHash`, `PerCPUArray`, `LRUCPUHash`, `PerCPUCGroupStorage`), the value type must additionally implement `MapPerCPUValue`:\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing\n    // MapValue. The slice length must equal the number of possible CPUs.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n### KeyValue (for StateDB Reconciler)\n\nThe `KeyValue` interface is used with the `NewMapOps` reconciler integration and is separate from the `MapKey`/`MapValue` interfaces:\n\n```go\ntype KeyValue interface {\n    BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n    BinaryValue() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n}\n```\n\n### StructBinaryMarshaler\n\nA convenience type for implementing `encoding.BinaryMarshaler` on structs of primitive fields:\n\n```go\ntype StructBinaryMarshaler struct {\n    Target any // pointer to struct\n}\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n\n```go\nfunc (x *MyKey) BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler {\n    return bpf.StructBinaryMarshaler{x}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map struct\n\nThe `Map` struct is the central type representing a BPF map. It wraps an underlying `ebpf.Map` and provides thread-safe operations, optional caching, metrics, and event buffering.\n\n**Exported fields:**\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n### NewMap\n\nCreates a new `Map` instance. This does **not** create the map in the kernel; it only constructs the in-memory representation with a `MapSpec`. The map must be opened or created before use via `OpenOrCreate()`, `Open()`, or `CreateUnpinned()`.\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The map name. Used to derive the pin path and as the BPF map name.\n- `mapType`: The BPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`, `ebpf.LRUHash`, `ebpf.Array`).\n- `mapKey`: A pointer to a zero-value instance of the key type (must implement `MapKey`).\n- `mapValue`: A pointer to a zero-value instance of the value type (must implement `MapValue`).\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold.\n- `flags`: BPF map creation flags (e.g., `BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Key and value sizes are computed via reflection from the provided `mapKey` and `mapValue` types.\n- The `Map` holds an `ebpf.MapSpec` until the map is created, at which point the spec is consumed and set to nil.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\n    \"cilium_my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &MyKey{},\n    &MyValue{},\n    1024,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\nLike `NewMap`, but also takes an `*ebpf.MapSpec` for the inner map. Used for map-of-maps types (`HashOfMaps`, `ArrayOfMaps`).\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\n### OpenMap\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map file on the BPF filesystem.\n- `key`: A zero-value instance of the key type.\n- `value`: A zero-value instance of the value type.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Returns an error if `pinPath` is not absolute.\n- The returned map is immediately usable; no call to `Open()` or `OpenOrCreate()` is needed.\n- The map is automatically registered in the global map registry.\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map or create a new one if it does not exist. If an existing map has incompatible attributes (type, key/value size, capacity, flags), it is deleted and recreated \u2014 **data in the old map is lost**.\n\nThe map is pinned to the BPF filesystem at the path derived from its name.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- If the map is already open (`m.m != nil`), this is a no-op.\n- Memory flags appropriate for the map type are automatically applied.\n- After successful creation, the internal `MapSpec` is consumed (set to nil) and cannot be reused.\n- The map is registered in the global map registry.\n\n### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map in the kernel **without** pinning it to the BPF filesystem. The map exists only as long as there are references to it (file descriptors, BPF programs).\n\n### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nCalls `OpenOrCreate()` to create or open the map (with pinning), then immediately closes it. Useful for ensuring a map exists on the filesystem without keeping a file descriptor open.\n\n### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an already-pinned map by loading it from the BPF filesystem path. This is a no-op if the map is already open. Use this when you know the map already exists and has been pinned.\n\n### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map's file descriptor and unregisters it from the global map registry. If the map has synchronization controllers enabled (via `WithCache()`), they are removed.\n\n### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves the pin at the map's path, then recreates the map and re-pins it. The map must not already be open (returns an error if `m.m != nil`). This effectively replaces an existing map with a fresh one.\n\n### IsOpen\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the map's file descriptor is currently open.\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nReads the value associated with `key` from the kernel map. Opens the map first if it is not already open.\n\n**Returns:** A newly allocated `MapValue` containing the result, or an error. Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` (wrapped) if the key is not found.\n\n### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates the entry for `key` with `value` in the kernel map. Uses `ebpf.UpdateAny` semantics (create or overwrite).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Opens the map if not already open.\n- If a cache is enabled (`WithCache()`), the cache entry is updated. On error, the entry is marked for retry via the error resolver.\n- If the event buffer is enabled, a `MapUpdate` event is recorded.\n\n### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry for `key` from the kernel map. Returns an error if the key does not exist.\n\n### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nLike `Delete`, but returns `(false, nil)` instead of an error when the key does not exist. Useful for cleanup paths where missing entries are expected.\n\n### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes an entry **without acquiring the map's lock**. This method **must only** be called from within a `DumpReliablyWithCallback` callback, where the lock is already held. Calling it outside this context will cause a data race.\n\n**Why this exists:** `DumpReliablyWithCallback` acquires a write lock for the duration of the iteration. If the callback needs to delete entries (e.g., during garbage collection), it must use `DeleteLocked` to avoid deadlock.\n\n### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in the map and deletes them one by one. If entries are being concurrently added during traversal, those entries may survive deletion.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- If a value cache is enabled, all entries are first marked for deletion.\n- A `MapDeleteAll` event is recorded in the event buffer.\n\n### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nResets all values in the map to their zero value without removing entries. Does not support maps with event buffers or value caches enabled (returns an error if either is active). Useful for array-type maps where you want to zero out values.\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### DumpCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n```\n\nCallback type used by the various `Dump*` methods. Each invocation receives newly allocated key/value instances that are safe to retain.\n\n### DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries, calling `cb` for each one. Opens the map if needed. Key and value instances passed to the callback are freshly allocated on each iteration and safe to retain.\n\n**Not safe for per-CPU maps.** Use `DumpPerCPUWithCallback` instead.\n\n### DumpPerCPUWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map. The `values` parameter is a slice (one element per CPU) of the value type, allocated via `MapPerCPUValue.NewSlice()`. Returns an error if the map is not a per-CPU type or the value does not implement `MapPerCPUValue`.\n\n### DumpWithCallbackIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback`, but returns `nil` without error if the map does not exist on the filesystem.\n\n### DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nProvides resilient iteration over maps that may be concurrently modified. Unlike `DumpWithCallback`, this method:\n\n- Tracks the current and previously seen keys so that if an element is deleted during iteration, traversal can continue from a nearby key rather than restarting.\n- Caps the maximum number of iterations at `4 * MaxEntries` to prevent infinite loops on continuously modified maps. Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if this limit is reached.\n- Acquires a **write lock** for the entire duration of the dump. Callbacks **must not** call `Update()`, `Delete()`, or `SilentDelete()` (they acquire the same lock). Use `DeleteLocked()` instead for deletions within the callback.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Must not be nil.\n- `stats`: Must be initialized via `NewDumpStats(m)`. Tracks iteration statistics.\n\n### Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nConvenience method that dumps all entries into a `map[string][]string`, using `key.String()` and `value.String()` for conversion.\n\n### DumpIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump`, but returns `nil` if the map file does not exist on the filesystem.\n\n---\n\n## Batch Iterator\n\nThe `BatchIterator` provides typed, batched iteration over BPF maps using the kernel's batch lookup API. It is more efficient than single-key iteration for large maps.\n\n### Type Definition\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n**Type constraints:**\n\n```go\ntype KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n    MapKey\n    *T\n}\n\ntype ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n    MapValue\n    *T\n}\n```\n\nThe pointer type of `KT` must implement `MapKey`, and the pointer type of `VT` must implement `MapValue`.\n\n### NewBatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for the given map.\n\n**Supported map types:** `Hash`, `LRUHash`, `LPMTrie`. Returns an error via `Err()` for other map types.\n\n### IterateAll\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns a Go 1.23+ range iterator (`iter.Seq2`) that yields all key/value pairs from the map using batched lookups.\n\n**ENOSPC retry behavior:** The batch buffer starts at a dynamically computed chunk size based on `sqrt(MaxEntries * 2)`. If a batch lookup fails with `ENOSPC` (buffer too small for the largest hash bucket), the buffer is doubled and the same batch is retried. This happens up to 3 times by default (configurable via `WithMaxRetries`). If all retries are exhausted, iteration stops and `Err()` returns the error.\n\n**Context cancellation:** Iteration stops if the context is cancelled, and `Err()` returns the context error.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_test\", ebpf.Hash, &TestKey{}, &TestValue{}, 1024, unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\niter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"key=%d value=%d\\n\", k.Key, v.Value)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### Err\n\n```go\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns any error encountered during the most recent `IterateAll()` call. Reset on each new call to `IterateAll()`.\n\n### Iterator Options\n\n#### WithMaxRetries\n\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the default maximum retries (3) when ENOSPC is encountered.\n\n#### WithStartingChunkSize\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the dynamically chosen starting chunk size. Minimum is 8.\n\n#### WithEBPFBatchOpts\n\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the `ebpf.BatchOptions` used for `BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH`.\n\n### CountAll\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nHelper that iterates the entire map and returns the total entry count.\n\n### BatchCount (on Map)\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts map entries using batch lookup without deserializing keys/values. Only supports `Hash`, `LRUHash`, and `LPMTrie` map types.\n\n### BatchLookup (on Map)\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any, opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nLow-level batch lookup wrapper. Returns the number of entries read in this batch.\n\n---\n\n## DumpStats\n\nTracks statistics over the traversal of a map via `DumpReliablyWithCallback`.\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started          time.Time\n    Finished         time.Time\n    Lookup           uint32  // Total key lookups performed\n    LookupFailed     uint32  // Key lookups that failed (key deleted mid-iteration)\n    PrevKeyUnavailable uint32\n    KeyFallback      uint32  // Times iteration fell back to a previous key\n    MaxEntries       uint32  // Maximum entries in the map\n    Interrupted      uint32  // Times iteration restarted from scratch\n    Completed        bool    // Whether iteration completed normally\n}\n```\n\n### NewDumpStats\n\n```go\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\n```\n\nReturns a new `DumpStats` initialized with the map's `MaxEntries`. Pass this to `DumpReliablyWithCallback`.\n\n### Duration\n\n```go\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\nReturns the wall-clock duration of the dump.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\nBPF maps can be pinned to the BPF filesystem (`bpffs`), which allows them to persist across process restarts and be shared between programs.\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n```go\n// BPFFSRoot returns the root path of the mounted BPF filesystem.\n// Default: /sys/fs/bpf\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n\n// CiliumPath returns the path used for Cilium-specific object pins.\n// Returns: <BPFFSRoot>/cilium\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n\n// MapPath returns the full filesystem path for a BPF map with the given name.\n// Returns: <BPFFSRoot>/tc/globals/<name>  (when running as cilium-agent)\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n\n// LocalMapName returns a map name scoped to a specific endpoint ID.\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n\n// LocalMapPath returns the full path for an endpoint-scoped map.\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n### CheckOrMountFS\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\nChecks if the BPF filesystem is mounted at the given root (or the default location). If not, mounts it. This is called once during initialization. If `bpfRoot` is empty or equals the default (`/sys/fs/bpf`), standard locations are checked.\n\n### Pin and Unpin Operations\n\nMaps are pinned automatically when created via `OpenOrCreate()`. Manual pin/unpin:\n\n```go\n// Unpin removes the map's pin from the filesystem.\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n\n// UnpinIfExists removes the pin only if the map file exists. No error on missing maps.\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n\n// Path returns the filesystem path for this map. Derives from name if not set.\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\n**Pinning behavior summary:**\n\n| Method | Pinned? | Notes |\n|--------|---------|-------|\n| `OpenOrCreate()` | Yes | Pin path derived from map name |\n| `CreateUnpinned()` | No | Map exists only while FDs are open |\n| `Create()` | Yes | Pins, then closes FD (pin keeps map alive) |\n| `OpenMap(pinPath, ...)` | Already pinned | Opens existing pin |\n| `Recreate()` | Yes | Removes old pin, creates new map, re-pins |\n\n### OpenOrCreateMap (Low-Level)\n\n```go\nfunc OpenOrCreateMap(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.MapSpec, pinDir string) (*ebpf.Map, error)\n```\n\nLow-level function that creates an `ebpf.Map` from a spec, handling pinning and incompatible map upgrades. If a pinned map exists but is incompatible with the spec, it is unpinned and recreated.\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\nThe event system provides an auditing buffer that records map operations (`Update`, `Delete`, `DeleteAll`) and supports real-time streaming via subscriptions.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer for the map. The config specifies:\n- `Enabled`: Whether to enable the buffer.\n- `MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to retain (ring buffer). Memory usage is approximately proportional to 100MB per million entries.\n- `TTL`: If non-zero, events older than this duration are periodically garbage collected.\n\nMust be called before the map is opened. Returns `m` for chaining.\n\n### Event Type\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // unexported: action, cacheEntry\n}\n```\n\n**Methods on Event:**\n\n```go\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string     // \"update\", \"delete\", or \"delete-all\"\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string         // String representation of the key, or \"<nil>\"\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string       // String representation of the value, or \"<nil>\"\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error    // Error from the operation, if any\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction // OK, Insert, or Delete\n```\n\n### Action Constants\n\n```go\nconst (\n    MapUpdate    Action = iota  // map.Update event\n    MapDelete                   // map.Delete event\n    MapDeleteAll                // map.DeleteAll event (aggregated)\n)\n```\n\n### EventCallbackFunc\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(*Event)\n```\n\nCallback for dumping buffered events.\n\n### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool) (*Handle, error)\n```\n\nAtomically dumps existing buffered events and (optionally) subscribes to future events. The dump and subscription happen under the same lock to prevent missed events between the two operations.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback`: If non-nil, called for each existing buffered event. Events older than the configured TTL are skipped.\n- `follow`: If `true`, a subscription `Handle` is returned for streaming future events.\n\n**Returns:** A `*Handle` for the subscription (only if `follow` is true), or an error.\n\n**Errors:**\n- Returns an error if events are not enabled on the map.\n- Returns an error if the maximum number of concurrent subscriptions (32) is exceeded.\n\n### Handle\n\n```go\ntype Handle struct {\n    // unexported fields\n}\n```\n\nRepresents an active subscription to map events.\n\n```go\n// C returns a read-only channel of events.\nfunc (h *Handle) C() <-chan *Event\n\n// Close safely closes the subscription handle and its channel.\nfunc (h *Handle) Close()\n```\n\n**Lifecycle and backpressure:**\n- The event channel has a buffer size of 32.\n- If a subscriber's channel buffer is full when a new event arrives, the subscription is **automatically closed** with an error. This prevents slow consumers from blocking map operations.\n- Always read from `h.C()` promptly or call `h.Close()` to stop receiving events.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\n// Dump existing events and subscribe to new ones.\nhandle, err := m.DumpAndSubscribe(func(e *bpf.Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"buffered: %s %s=%s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n}, true)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer handle.Close()\n\n// Process live events.\nfor event := range handle.C() {\n    fmt.Printf(\"live: %s %s=%s\\n\", event.GetAction(), event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n}\n```\n\n### IsEventsEnabled\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThese functions load eBPF ELF objects (compiled BPF C programs with maps) into the kernel.\n\n### LoadCollectionSpec\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollectionSpec(logger *slog.Logger, path string) (*ebpf.CollectionSpec, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF ELF file and parses it into an `ebpf.CollectionSpec`. This is a blueprint \u2014 no kernel resources are created.\n\n**Additional processing beyond `ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec`:**\n- Validates that all programs have a specified type (no `UnspecifiedProgram`).\n- Performs static reachability analysis of tail call programs: any tail call not reachable from an entrypoint program is removed from the spec.\n- Resolves tail calls by populating the `cilium_calls` program array map.\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads a `CollectionSpec` into the kernel, returning the live `Collection` and a **commit function**.\n\n**The commit function** must be called **after** the collection's entrypoint programs are attached to their kernel hooks (TC, XDP, etc.). It replaces bpffs pins for maps that were found to be incompatible with their pinned counterparts, or maps with the `CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE` flag.\n\n**Why deferred pinning?** Replacing tail call map pins before programs are attached would cause a window where programs reference the old map while the new one is pinned. The commit function ensures atomic switchover.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `spec`: Must not be nil. A copy is made internally so the caller can safely reuse the original.\n- `opts`: Optional `CollectionOptions`.\n\n**Verifier log sizing:** The verifier log buffer starts at 4 MiB and quadruples on each retry (up to 5 attempts). If still insufficient, a truncated `ebpf.VerifierError` is returned.\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nConvenience wrapper that calls `LoadCollection` and then assigns the resulting eBPF objects to a struct. The struct fields should be tagged with `ebpf:\"name\"` to match programs and maps.\n\n**Returns:** The commit function (same as `LoadCollection`), or an error.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nspec, err := bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(logger, \"bpf_program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\nobjs := struct {\n    MyProgram *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"my_program\"`\n    MyMap     *ebpf.Map     `ebpf:\"my_map\"`\n}{}\n\ncommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(logger, &objs, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n    CollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n        Maps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.CiliumPath()},\n    },\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Attach objs.MyProgram to a hook...\n\n// After all programs are attached, commit map pin replacements.\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants holds runtime configuration values declared with DECLARE_CONFIG\n    // in BPF C code. Pass a pointer to a populated config struct.\n    Constants any\n\n    // MapRenames maps CollectionSpec.Maps keys to new names. Used to give maps\n    // unique bpffs pin paths (e.g., per-endpoint maps).\n    MapRenames map[string]string\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## EndpointKey\n\nA concrete example of a `MapKey` implementation used in Cilium for the endpoints BPF map.\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6  // Holds both IPv6 and IPv4 (in lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8       // EndpointKeyIPv4 (1) or EndpointKeyIPv6 (2)\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n```\n\n### NewEndpointKey\n\n```go\nfunc NewEndpointKey(ip net.IP, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey\n```\n\nCreates an `EndpointKey` from an IP address. The address family (`IPv4`/`IPv6`) is auto-detected from the IP.\n\n### String\n\n```go\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string\n```\n\nReturns a string like `\"10.0.0.1@0:0\"` (address\\@cluster:key).\n\n---\n\n## Map Memory Flags\n\nGlobal settings that affect memory allocation strategy for BPF maps.\n\n```go\n// EnableMapPreAllocation enables pre-allocation for supported map types.\nfunc EnableMapPreAllocation()\n\n// DisableMapPreAllocation sets BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC for hash-type maps (default).\nfunc DisableMapPreAllocation()\n\n// EnableMapDistributedLRU splits LRU backend memory across CPUs (BPF_F_NO_COMMON_LRU).\nfunc EnableMapDistributedLRU()\n\n// DisableMapDistributedLRU uses a shared LRU backend (default).\nfunc DisableMapDistributedLRU()\n\n// GetMapMemoryFlags returns the memory flags for a given map type based on\n// current global settings. Called automatically during map creation.\nfunc GetMapMemoryFlags(t ebpf.MapType) uint32\n```\n\n**Flag application by map type:**\n\n| Map Type | Pre-alloc Setting Applied | LRU Setting Applied |\n|----------|--------------------------|---------------------|\n| `Hash`, `PerCPUHash`, `HashOfMaps` | Yes | No |\n| `LRUHash`, `LRUCPUHash` | No | Yes |\n| `LPMTrie` | Always `NO_PREALLOC` | No |\n| Others (Array, etc.) | No | No |\n\n---\n\n## Map Builder Pattern\n\nMaps support a builder pattern for configuring optional features before opening:\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1024, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{Enabled: true, MaxSize: 1000}).\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithGroupName(\"my_group\")\n```\n\n### WithCache\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables a local cache that tracks all user-space insertions and deletions. Failed operations are retried by a periodic error resolver controller. The cache stores entries keyed by `MapKey.String()`.\n\n### WithEvents\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer (see [Event System](#event-system)).\n\n### WithPressureMetric / WithPressureMetricThreshold\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\n```\n\nEnables a metric that tracks map pressure (ratio of entries to max capacity). `WithPressureMetricThreshold` only reports the metric when pressure exceeds the given threshold. Enabling pressure metrics implicitly enables key tracking in the cache.\n\n### WithGroupName\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nSets the metric group name for the map, used to classify maps of the same type for aggregate metrics.\n\n---\n\n## Map Accessor Methods\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string              // Returns the basename of the map\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType        // Returns the BPF map type\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32           // Returns the key size in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32         // Returns the value size in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32        // Returns the maximum number of entries\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32             // Returns the map creation flags\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int                   // Returns the file descriptor (map must be open)\nfunc (m *Map) NonPrefixedName() string   // Returns name without \"cilium_\" prefix\n```\n\n---\n\n## Map Registry\n\nA global registry tracks all open maps for introspection.\n\n```go\n// GetMap returns the registered map by name or absolute path.\nfunc GetMap(logger *slog.Logger, name string) *Map\n\n// GetOpenMaps returns API models of all currently open maps.\nfunc GetOpenMaps() []*models.BPFMap\n\n// GetModel returns the API model for a single map.\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\n---\n\n## StateDB Reconciler Integration\n\nThe `NewMapOps` function bridges BPF maps with Cilium's StateDB reconciler:\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapOps[KV KeyValue](m *Map) reconciler.Operations[KV]\n```\n\nReturns a `reconciler.Operations` implementation backed by the BPF map. The reconciler will call `Update`, `Delete`, and `Prune` to keep the BPF map in sync with a StateDB table.\n\n**Error:** Returns `ErrMapNotOpened` if the map has not been opened before the reconciler starts.\n",
