{
  "content": "# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference\n\nThe `bpf` package provides Go wrappers for interacting with kernel eBPF maps from user space. It offers a high-level API for creating, reading, updating, and deleting map entries, as well as facilities for map pinning, event streaming, batch iteration, and eBPF collection loading.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)\n2. [Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)\n3. [Map Lifecycle Operations](#map-lifecycle-operations)\n4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)\n5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)\n6. [Batch Iterator](#batch-iterator)\n7. [DumpStats](#dumpstats)\n8. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)\n9. [Event System](#event-system)\n10. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)\n11. [EndpointKey (Concrete Key Example)](#endpointkey)\n12. [Map Memory Flags](#map-memory-flags)\n\n---\n\n## Key/Value Interfaces\n\nAll map operations are typed through these interfaces. Any type used as a key or value in a `Map` must implement the corresponding interface.\n\n### MapKey\n\n```go\ntype MapKey interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapKey of the same\n    // concrete type. Used internally to allocate buffers for iteration\n    // and lookup.\n    New() MapKey\n}\n```\n\n### MapValue\n\n```go\ntype MapValue interface {\n    fmt.Stringer\n\n    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapValue of the same\n    // concrete type.\n    New() MapValue\n}\n```\n\n### MapPerCPUValue\n\nFor per-CPU map types (`PerCPUHash`, `PerCPUArray`, `LRUCPUHash`, `PerCPUCGroupStorage`), the value type must additionally implement `MapPerCPUValue`:\n\n```go\ntype MapPerCPUValue interface {\n    MapValue\n\n    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing\n    // MapValue. The slice length must equal the number of possible CPUs.\n    NewSlice() any\n}\n```\n\n### KeyValue (for StateDB Reconciler)\n\nThe `KeyValue` interface is used with the `NewMapOps` reconciler integration and is separate from the `MapKey`/`MapValue` interfaces:\n\n```go\ntype KeyValue interface {\n    BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n    BinaryValue() encoding.BinaryMarshaler\n}\n```\n\n### StructBinaryMarshaler\n\nA convenience type for implementing `encoding.BinaryMarshaler` on structs of primitive fields:\n\n```go\ntype StructBinaryMarshaler struct {\n    Target any // pointer to struct\n}\n```\n\n**Usage:**\n\n```go\nfunc (x *MyKey) BinaryKey() encoding.BinaryMarshaler {\n    return bpf.StructBinaryMarshaler{x}\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Core Map Type and Creation\n\n### Map struct\n\nThe `Map` struct is the central type representing a BPF map. It wraps an underlying `ebpf.Map` and provides thread-safe operations, optional caching, metrics, and event buffering.\n\n**Exported fields:**\n\n```go\ntype Map struct {\n    Logger *slog.Logger\n    // ... unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n### NewMap\n\nCreates a new `Map` instance. This does **not** create the map in the kernel; it only constructs the in-memory representation with a `MapSpec`. The map must be opened or created before use via `OpenOrCreate()`, `Open()`, or `CreateUnpinned()`.\n\n```go\nfunc NewMap(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32) *Map\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name`: The map name. Used to derive the pin path and as the BPF map name.\n- `mapType`: The BPF map type (e.g., `ebpf.Hash`, `ebpf.LRUHash`, `ebpf.Array`).\n- `mapKey`: A pointer to a zero-value instance of the key type (must implement `MapKey`).\n- `mapValue`: A pointer to a zero-value instance of the value type (must implement `MapValue`).\n- `maxEntries`: Maximum number of entries the map can hold.\n- `flags`: BPF map creation flags (e.g., `BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC`).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Key and value sizes are computed via reflection from the provided `mapKey` and `mapValue` types.\n- The `Map` holds an `ebpf.MapSpec` until the map is created, at which point the spec is consumed and set to nil.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\n    \"cilium_my_map\",\n    ebpf.Hash,\n    &MyKey{},\n    &MyValue{},\n    1024,\n    unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC,\n)\n```\n\n### NewMapWithInnerSpec\n\nLike `NewMap`, but also takes an `*ebpf.MapSpec` for the inner map. Used for map-of-maps types (`HashOfMaps`, `ArrayOfMaps`).\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapWithInnerSpec(name string, mapType ebpf.MapType, mapKey MapKey, mapValue MapValue,\n    maxEntries int, flags uint32, innerSpec *ebpf.MapSpec) *Map\n```\n\n### OpenMap\n\nOpens an existing pinned map from the BPF filesystem.\n\n```go\nfunc OpenMap(pinPath string, key MapKey, value MapValue) (*Map, error)\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `pinPath`: Absolute path to the pinned map file on the BPF filesystem.\n- `key`: A zero-value instance of the key type.\n- `value`: A zero-value instance of the value type.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Returns an error if `pinPath` is not absolute.\n- The returned map is immediately usable; no call to `Open()` or `OpenOrCreate()` is needed.\n- The map is automatically registered in the global map registry.\n\n---\n\n## Map Lifecycle Operations\n\n### OpenOrCreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) OpenOrCreate() error\n```\n\nAttempts to open an existing pinned map or create a new one if it does not exist. If an existing map has incompatible attributes (type, key/value size, capacity, flags), it is deleted and recreated \u2014 **data in the old map is lost**.\n\nThe map is pinned to the BPF filesystem at the path derived from its name.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- If the map is already open (`m.m != nil`), this is a no-op.\n- Memory flags appropriate for the map type are automatically applied.\n- After successful creation, the internal `MapSpec` is consumed (set to nil) and cannot be reused.\n- The map is registered in the global map registry.\n\n### CreateUnpinned\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) CreateUnpinned() error\n```\n\nCreates the map in the kernel **without** pinning it to the BPF filesystem. The map exists only as long as there are references to it (file descriptors, BPF programs).\n\n### Create\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Create() error\n```\n\nCalls `OpenOrCreate()` to create or open the map (with pinning), then immediately closes it. Useful for ensuring a map exists on the filesystem without keeping a file descriptor open.\n\n### Open\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Open() error\n```\n\nOpens an already-pinned map by loading it from the BPF filesystem path. This is a no-op if the map is already open. Use this when you know the map already exists and has been pinned.\n\n### Close\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Close() error\n```\n\nCloses the map's file descriptor and unregisters it from the global map registry. If the map has synchronization controllers enabled (via `WithCache()`), they are removed.\n\n### Recreate\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Recreate() error\n```\n\nRemoves the pin at the map's path, then recreates the map and re-pins it. The map must not already be open (returns an error if `m.m != nil`). This effectively replaces an existing map with a fresh one.\n\n### IsOpen\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsOpen() bool\n```\n\nReturns `true` if the map's file descriptor is currently open.\n\n---\n\n## CRUD Operations\n\n### Lookup\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Lookup(key MapKey) (MapValue, error)\n```\n\nReads the value associated with `key` from the kernel map. Opens the map first if it is not already open.\n\n**Returns:** A newly allocated `MapValue` containing the result, or an error. Returns `ebpf.ErrKeyNotExist` (wrapped) if the key is not found.\n\n### Update\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Update(key MapKey, value MapValue) error\n```\n\nInserts or updates the entry for `key` with `value` in the kernel map. Uses `ebpf.UpdateAny` semantics (create or overwrite).\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- Opens the map if not already open.\n- If a cache is enabled (`WithCache()`), the cache entry is updated. On error, the entry is marked for retry via the error resolver.\n- If the event buffer is enabled, a `MapUpdate` event is recorded.\n\n### Delete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Delete(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes the entry for `key` from the kernel map. Returns an error if the key does not exist.\n\n### SilentDelete\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) SilentDelete(key MapKey) (deleted bool, err error)\n```\n\nLike `Delete`, but returns `(false, nil)` instead of an error when the key does not exist. Useful for cleanup paths where missing entries are expected.\n\n### DeleteLocked\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteLocked(key MapKey) error\n```\n\nDeletes an entry **without acquiring the map's lock**. This method **must only** be called from within a `DumpReliablyWithCallback` callback, where the lock is already held. Calling it outside this context will cause a data race.\n\n**Why this exists:** `DumpReliablyWithCallback` acquires a write lock for the duration of the iteration. If the callback needs to delete entries (e.g., during garbage collection), it must use `DeleteLocked` to avoid deadlock.\n\n### DeleteAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DeleteAll() error\n```\n\nIterates over all entries in the map and deletes them one by one. If entries are being concurrently added during traversal, those entries may survive deletion.\n\n**Behavioral notes:**\n- If a value cache is enabled, all entries are first marked for deletion.\n- A `MapDeleteAll` event is recorded in the event buffer.\n\n### ClearAll\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) ClearAll() error\n```\n\nResets all values in the map to their zero value without removing entries. Does not support maps with event buffers or value caches enabled (returns an error if either is active). Useful for array-type maps where you want to zero out values.\n\n---\n\n## Iteration and Dumping\n\n### DumpCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpCallback func(key MapKey, value MapValue)\n```\n\nCallback type used by the various `Dump*` methods. Each invocation receives newly allocated key/value instances that are safe to retain.\n\n### DumpWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallback(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over all map entries, calling `cb` for each one. Opens the map if needed. Key and value instances passed to the callback are freshly allocated on each iteration and safe to retain.\n\n**Not safe for per-CPU maps.** Use `DumpPerCPUWithCallback` instead.\n\n### DumpPerCPUWithCallback\n\n```go\ntype DumpPerCPUCallback func(key MapKey, values any)\n\nfunc (m *Map) DumpPerCPUWithCallback(cb DumpPerCPUCallback) error\n```\n\nIterates over a per-CPU map. The `values` parameter is a slice (one element per CPU) of the value type, allocated via `MapPerCPUValue.NewSlice()`. Returns an error if the map is not a per-CPU type or the value does not implement `MapPerCPUValue`.\n\n### DumpWithCallbackIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpWithCallbackIfExists(cb DumpCallback) error\n```\n\nLike `DumpWithCallback`, but returns `nil` without error if the map does not exist on the filesystem.\n\n### DumpReliablyWithCallback\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpReliablyWithCallback(cb DumpCallback, stats *DumpStats) error\n```\n\nProvides resilient iteration over maps that may be concurrently modified. Unlike `DumpWithCallback`, this method:\n\n- Tracks the current and previously seen keys so that if an element is deleted during iteration, traversal can continue from a nearby key rather than restarting.\n- Caps the maximum number of iterations at `4 * MaxEntries` to prevent infinite loops on continuously modified maps. Returns `ErrMaxLookup` if this limit is reached.\n- Acquires a **write lock** for the entire duration of the dump. Callbacks **must not** call `Update()`, `Delete()`, or `SilentDelete()` (they acquire the same lock). Use `DeleteLocked()` instead for deletions within the callback.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `cb`: Must not be nil.\n- `stats`: Must be initialized via `NewDumpStats(m)`. Tracks iteration statistics.\n\n### Dump\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Dump(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nConvenience method that dumps all entries into a `map[string][]string`, using `key.String()` and `value.String()` for conversion.\n\n### DumpIfExists\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpIfExists(hash map[string][]string) error\n```\n\nLike `Dump`, but returns `nil` if the map file does not exist on the filesystem.\n\n---\n\n## Batch Iterator\n\nThe `BatchIterator` provides typed, batched iteration over BPF maps using the kernel's batch lookup API. It is more efficient than single-key iteration for large maps.\n\n### Type Definition\n\n```go\ntype BatchIterator[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]] struct {\n    // unexported fields\n}\n```\n\n**Type constraints:**\n\n```go\ntype KeyPointer[T any] interface {\n    MapKey\n    *T\n}\n\ntype ValuePointer[T any] interface {\n    MapValue\n    *T\n}\n```\n\nThe pointer type of `KT` must implement `MapKey`, and the pointer type of `VT` must implement `MapValue`.\n\n### NewBatchIterator\n\n```go\nfunc NewBatchIterator[KT any, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](m *Map) *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nCreates a new batch iterator for the given map.\n\n**Supported map types:** `Hash`, `LRUHash`, `LPMTrie`. Returns an error via `Err()` for other map types.\n\n### IterateAll\n\n```go\nfunc (bi *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) IterateAll(ctx context.Context, opts ...BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]) iter.Seq2[KP, VP]\n```\n\nReturns a Go 1.23+ range iterator (`iter.Seq2`) that yields all key/value pairs from the map using batched lookups.\n\n**ENOSPC retry behavior:** The batch buffer starts at a dynamically computed chunk size based on `sqrt(MaxEntries * 2)`. If a batch lookup fails with `ENOSPC` (buffer too small for the largest hash bucket), the buffer is doubled and the same batch is retried. This happens up to 3 times by default (configurable via `WithMaxRetries`). If all retries are exhausted, iteration stops and `Err()` returns the error.\n\n**Context cancellation:** Iteration stops if the context is cancelled, and `Err()` returns the context error.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"cilium_test\", ebpf.Hash, &TestKey{}, &TestValue{}, 1024, unix.BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC)\nif err := m.OpenOrCreate(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\niter := bpf.NewBatchIterator[TestKey, TestValue](m)\nfor k, v := range iter.IterateAll(context.TODO()) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"key=%d value=%d\\n\", k.Key, v.Value)\n}\nif err := iter.Err(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### Err\n\n```go\nfunc (bi BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) Err() error\n```\n\nReturns any error encountered during the most recent `IterateAll()` call. Reset on each new call to `IterateAll()`.\n\n### Iterator Options\n\n#### WithMaxRetries\n\n```go\nfunc WithMaxRetries[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](retries uint32) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the default maximum retries (3) when ENOSPC is encountered.\n\n#### WithStartingChunkSize\n\n```go\nfunc WithStartingChunkSize[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](size int) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the dynamically chosen starting chunk size. Minimum is 8.\n\n#### WithEBPFBatchOpts\n\n```go\nfunc WithEBPFBatchOpts[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) BatchIteratorOpt[KT, VT, KP, VP]\n```\n\nOverrides the `ebpf.BatchOptions` used for `BPF_MAP_LOOKUP_BATCH`.\n\n### CountAll\n\n```go\nfunc CountAll[KT, VT any, KP KeyPointer[KT], VP ValuePointer[VT]](ctx context.Context, iter *BatchIterator[KT, VT, KP, VP]) (int, error)\n```\n\nHelper that iterates the entire map and returns the total entry count.\n\n### BatchCount (on Map)\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchCount() (count int, err error)\n```\n\nCounts map entries using batch lookup without deserializing keys/values. Only supports `Hash`, `LRUHash`, and `LPMTrie` map types.\n\n### BatchLookup (on Map)\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) BatchLookup(cursor *ebpf.MapBatchCursor, keysOut, valuesOut any, opts *ebpf.BatchOptions) (int, error)\n```\n\nLow-level batch lookup wrapper. Returns the number of entries read in this batch.\n\n---\n\n## DumpStats\n\nTracks statistics over the traversal of a map via `DumpReliablyWithCallback`.\n\n```go\ntype DumpStats struct {\n    Started          time.Time\n    Finished         time.Time\n    Lookup           uint32  // Total key lookups performed\n    LookupFailed     uint32  // Key lookups that failed (key deleted mid-iteration)\n    PrevKeyUnavailable uint32\n    KeyFallback      uint32  // Times iteration fell back to a previous key\n    MaxEntries       uint32  // Maximum entries in the map\n    Interrupted      uint32  // Times iteration restarted from scratch\n    Completed        bool    // Whether iteration completed normally\n}\n```\n\n### NewDumpStats\n\n```go\nfunc NewDumpStats(m *Map) *DumpStats\n```\n\nReturns a new `DumpStats` initialized with the map's `MaxEntries`. Pass this to `DumpReliablyWithCallback`.\n\n### Duration\n\n```go\nfunc (d *DumpStats) Duration() time.Duration\n```\n\nReturns the wall-clock duration of the dump.\n\n---\n\n## Pinning and Persistence\n\nBPF maps can be pinned to the BPF filesystem (`bpffs`), which allows them to persist across process restarts and be shared between programs.\n\n### BPF Filesystem Paths\n\n```go\n// BPFFSRoot returns the root path of the mounted BPF filesystem.\n// Default: /sys/fs/bpf\nfunc BPFFSRoot() string\n\n// CiliumPath returns the path used for Cilium-specific object pins.\n// Returns: <BPFFSRoot>/cilium\nfunc CiliumPath() string\n\n// MapPath returns the full filesystem path for a BPF map with the given name.\n// Returns: <BPFFSRoot>/tc/globals/<name>  (when running as cilium-agent)\nfunc MapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string) string\n\n// LocalMapName returns a map name scoped to a specific endpoint ID.\nfunc LocalMapName(name string, id uint16) string\n\n// LocalMapPath returns the full path for an endpoint-scoped map.\nfunc LocalMapPath(logger *slog.Logger, name string, id uint16) string\n```\n\n### CheckOrMountFS\n\n```go\nfunc CheckOrMountFS(logger *slog.Logger, bpfRoot string)\n```\n\nChecks if the BPF filesystem is mounted at the given root (or the default location). If not, mounts it. This is called once during initialization. If `bpfRoot` is empty or equals the default (`/sys/fs/bpf`), standard locations are checked.\n\n### Pin and Unpin Operations\n\nMaps are pinned automatically when created via `OpenOrCreate()`. Manual pin/unpin:\n\n```go\n// Unpin removes the map's pin from the filesystem.\nfunc (m *Map) Unpin() error\n\n// UnpinIfExists removes the pin only if the map file exists. No error on missing maps.\nfunc (m *Map) UnpinIfExists() error\n\n// Path returns the filesystem path for this map. Derives from name if not set.\nfunc (m *Map) Path() (string, error)\n```\n\n**Pinning behavior summary:**\n\n| Method | Pinned? | Notes |\n|--------|---------|-------|\n| `OpenOrCreate()` | Yes | Pin path derived from map name |\n| `CreateUnpinned()` | No | Map exists only while FDs are open |\n| `Create()` | Yes | Pins, then closes FD (pin keeps map alive) |\n| `OpenMap(pinPath, ...)` | Already pinned | Opens existing pin |\n| `Recreate()` | Yes | Removes old pin, creates new map, re-pins |\n\n### OpenOrCreateMap (Low-Level)\n\n```go\nfunc OpenOrCreateMap(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.MapSpec, pinDir string) (*ebpf.Map, error)\n```\n\nLow-level function that creates an `ebpf.Map` from a spec, handling pinning and incompatible map upgrades. If a pinned map exists but is incompatible with the spec, it is unpinned and recreated.\n\n---\n\n## Event System\n\nThe event system provides an auditing buffer that records map operations (`Update`, `Delete`, `DeleteAll`) and supports real-time streaming via subscriptions.\n\n### Enabling Events\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer for the map. The config specifies:\n- `Enabled`: Whether to enable the buffer.\n- `MaxSize`: Maximum number of events to retain (ring buffer). Memory usage is approximately proportional to 100MB per million entries.\n- `TTL`: If non-zero, events older than this duration are periodically garbage collected.\n\nMust be called before the map is opened. Returns `m` for chaining.\n\n### Event Type\n\n```go\ntype Event struct {\n    Timestamp time.Time\n    // unexported: action, cacheEntry\n}\n```\n\n**Methods on Event:**\n\n```go\nfunc (e *Event) GetAction() string     // \"update\", \"delete\", or \"delete-all\"\nfunc (e Event) GetKey() string         // String representation of the key, or \"<nil>\"\nfunc (e Event) GetValue() string       // String representation of the value, or \"<nil>\"\nfunc (e Event) GetLastError() error    // Error from the operation, if any\nfunc (e Event) GetDesiredAction() DesiredAction // OK, Insert, or Delete\n```\n\n### Action Constants\n\n```go\nconst (\n    MapUpdate    Action = iota  // map.Update event\n    MapDelete                   // map.Delete event\n    MapDeleteAll                // map.DeleteAll event (aggregated)\n)\n```\n\n### EventCallbackFunc\n\n```go\ntype EventCallbackFunc func(*Event)\n```\n\nCallback for dumping buffered events.\n\n### DumpAndSubscribe\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) DumpAndSubscribe(callback EventCallbackFunc, follow bool) (*Handle, error)\n```\n\nAtomically dumps existing buffered events and (optionally) subscribes to future events. The dump and subscription happen under the same lock to prevent missed events between the two operations.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback`: If non-nil, called for each existing buffered event. Events older than the configured TTL are skipped.\n- `follow`: If `true`, a subscription `Handle` is returned for streaming future events.\n\n**Returns:** A `*Handle` for the subscription (only if `follow` is true), or an error.\n\n**Errors:**\n- Returns an error if events are not enabled on the map.\n- Returns an error if the maximum number of concurrent subscriptions (32) is exceeded.\n\n### Handle\n\n```go\ntype Handle struct {\n    // unexported fields\n}\n```\n\nRepresents an active subscription to map events.\n\n```go\n// C returns a read-only channel of events.\nfunc (h *Handle) C() <-chan *Event\n\n// Close safely closes the subscription handle and its channel.\nfunc (h *Handle) Close()\n```\n\n**Lifecycle and backpressure:**\n- The event channel has a buffer size of 32.\n- If a subscriber's channel buffer is full when a new event arrives, the subscription is **automatically closed** with an error. This prevents slow consumers from blocking map operations.\n- Always read from `h.C()` promptly or call `h.Close()` to stop receiving events.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\n// Dump existing events and subscribe to new ones.\nhandle, err := m.DumpAndSubscribe(func(e *bpf.Event) {\n    fmt.Printf(\"buffered: %s %s=%s\\n\", e.GetAction(), e.GetKey(), e.GetValue())\n}, true)\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\ndefer handle.Close()\n\n// Process live events.\nfor event := range handle.C() {\n    fmt.Printf(\"live: %s %s=%s\\n\", event.GetAction(), event.GetKey(), event.GetValue())\n}\n```\n\n### IsEventsEnabled\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) IsEventsEnabled() bool\n```\n\nReturns whether the event buffer is enabled for this map.\n\n---\n\n## Collection Loading\n\nThese functions load eBPF ELF objects (compiled BPF C programs with maps) into the kernel.\n\n### LoadCollectionSpec\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollectionSpec(logger *slog.Logger, path string) (*ebpf.CollectionSpec, error)\n```\n\nLoads an eBPF ELF file and parses it into an `ebpf.CollectionSpec`. This is a blueprint \u2014 no kernel resources are created.\n\n**Additional processing beyond `ebpf.LoadCollectionSpec`:**\n- Validates that all programs have a specified type (no `UnspecifiedProgram`).\n- Performs static reachability analysis of tail call programs: any tail call not reachable from an entrypoint program is removed from the spec.\n- Resolves tail calls by populating the `cilium_calls` program array map.\n\n### LoadCollection\n\n```go\nfunc LoadCollection(logger *slog.Logger, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (*ebpf.Collection, func() error, error)\n```\n\nLoads a `CollectionSpec` into the kernel, returning the live `Collection` and a **commit function**.\n\n**The commit function** must be called **after** the collection's entrypoint programs are attached to their kernel hooks (TC, XDP, etc.). It replaces bpffs pins for maps that were found to be incompatible with their pinned counterparts, or maps with the `CILIUM_PIN_REPLACE` flag.\n\n**Why deferred pinning?** Replacing tail call map pins before programs are attached would cause a window where programs reference the old map while the new one is pinned. The commit function ensures atomic switchover.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `spec`: Must not be nil. A copy is made internally so the caller can safely reuse the original.\n- `opts`: Optional `CollectionOptions`.\n\n**Verifier log sizing:** The verifier log buffer starts at 4 MiB and quadruples on each retry (up to 5 attempts). If still insufficient, a truncated `ebpf.VerifierError` is returned.\n\n### LoadAndAssign\n\n```go\nfunc LoadAndAssign(logger *slog.Logger, to any, spec *ebpf.CollectionSpec, opts *CollectionOptions) (func() error, error)\n```\n\nConvenience wrapper that calls `LoadCollection` and then assigns the resulting eBPF objects to a struct. The struct fields should be tagged with `ebpf:\"name\"` to match programs and maps.\n\n**Returns:** The commit function (same as `LoadCollection`), or an error.\n\n**Example:**\n\n```go\nspec, err := bpf.LoadCollectionSpec(logger, \"bpf_program.o\")\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\nobjs := struct {\n    MyProgram *ebpf.Program `ebpf:\"my_program\"`\n    MyMap     *ebpf.Map     `ebpf:\"my_map\"`\n}{}\n\ncommit, err := bpf.LoadAndAssign(logger, &objs, spec, &bpf.CollectionOptions{\n    CollectionOptions: ebpf.CollectionOptions{\n        Maps: ebpf.MapOptions{PinPath: bpf.CiliumPath()},\n    },\n})\nif err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n\n// Attach objs.MyProgram to a hook...\n\n// After all programs are attached, commit map pin replacements.\nif err := commit(); err != nil {\n    log.Fatal(err)\n}\n```\n\n### CollectionOptions\n\n```go\ntype CollectionOptions struct {\n    ebpf.CollectionOptions\n\n    // Constants holds runtime configuration values declared with DECLARE_CONFIG\n    // in BPF C code. Pass a pointer to a populated config struct.\n    Constants any\n\n    // MapRenames maps CollectionSpec.Maps keys to new names. Used to give maps\n    // unique bpffs pin paths (e.g., per-endpoint maps).\n    MapRenames map[string]string\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## EndpointKey\n\nA concrete example of a `MapKey` implementation used in Cilium for the endpoints BPF map.\n\n```go\ntype EndpointKey struct {\n    IP        types.IPv6  // Holds both IPv6 and IPv4 (in lowest 4 bytes)\n    Family    uint8       // EndpointKeyIPv4 (1) or EndpointKeyIPv6 (2)\n    Key       uint8\n    ClusterID uint16\n}\n```\n\n### NewEndpointKey\n\n```go\nfunc NewEndpointKey(ip net.IP, clusterID uint16) EndpointKey\n```\n\nCreates an `EndpointKey` from an IP address. The address family (`IPv4`/`IPv6`) is auto-detected from the IP.\n\n### String\n\n```go\nfunc (k EndpointKey) String() string\n```\n\nReturns a string like `\"10.0.0.1@0:0\"` (address\\@cluster:key).\n\n---\n\n## Map Memory Flags\n\nGlobal settings that affect memory allocation strategy for BPF maps.\n\n```go\n// EnableMapPreAllocation enables pre-allocation for supported map types.\nfunc EnableMapPreAllocation()\n\n// DisableMapPreAllocation sets BPF_F_NO_PREALLOC for hash-type maps (default).\nfunc DisableMapPreAllocation()\n\n// EnableMapDistributedLRU splits LRU backend memory across CPUs (BPF_F_NO_COMMON_LRU).\nfunc EnableMapDistributedLRU()\n\n// DisableMapDistributedLRU uses a shared LRU backend (default).\nfunc DisableMapDistributedLRU()\n\n// GetMapMemoryFlags returns the memory flags for a given map type based on\n// current global settings. Called automatically during map creation.\nfunc GetMapMemoryFlags(t ebpf.MapType) uint32\n```\n\n**Flag application by map type:**\n\n| Map Type | Pre-alloc Setting Applied | LRU Setting Applied |\n|----------|--------------------------|---------------------|\n| `Hash`, `PerCPUHash`, `HashOfMaps` | Yes | No |\n| `LRUHash`, `LRUCPUHash` | No | Yes |\n| `LPMTrie` | Always `NO_PREALLOC` | No |\n| Others (Array, etc.) | No | No |\n\n---\n\n## Map Builder Pattern\n\nMaps support a builder pattern for configuring optional features before opening:\n\n```go\nm := bpf.NewMap(\"my_map\", ebpf.Hash, &Key{}, &Value{}, 1024, 0).\n    WithCache().\n    WithEvents(option.BPFEventBufferConfig{Enabled: true, MaxSize: 1000}).\n    WithPressureMetric(registry).\n    WithGroupName(\"my_group\")\n```\n\n### WithCache\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithCache() *Map\n```\n\nEnables a local cache that tracks all user-space insertions and deletions. Failed operations are retried by a periodic error resolver controller. The cache stores entries keyed by `MapKey.String()`.\n\n### WithEvents\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithEvents(c option.BPFEventBufferConfig) *Map\n```\n\nEnables the event buffer (see [Event System](#event-system)).\n\n### WithPressureMetric / WithPressureMetricThreshold\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetric(registry *metrics.Registry) *Map\nfunc (m *Map) WithPressureMetricThreshold(registry *metrics.Registry, threshold float64) *Map\n```\n\nEnables a metric that tracks map pressure (ratio of entries to max capacity). `WithPressureMetricThreshold` only reports the metric when pressure exceeds the given threshold. Enabling pressure metrics implicitly enables key tracking in the cache.\n\n### WithGroupName\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) WithGroupName(group string) *Map\n```\n\nSets the metric group name for the map, used to classify maps of the same type for aggregate metrics.\n\n---\n\n## Map Accessor Methods\n\n```go\nfunc (m *Map) Name() string              // Returns the basename of the map\nfunc (m *Map) Type() ebpf.MapType        // Returns the BPF map type\nfunc (m *Map) KeySize() uint32           // Returns the key size in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) ValueSize() uint32         // Returns the value size in bytes\nfunc (m *Map) MaxEntries() uint32        // Returns the maximum number of entries\nfunc (m *Map) Flags() uint32             // Returns the map creation flags\nfunc (m *Map) FD() int                   // Returns the file descriptor (map must be open)\nfunc (m *Map) NonPrefixedName() string   // Returns name without \"cilium_\" prefix\n```\n\n---\n\n## Map Registry\n\nA global registry tracks all open maps for introspection.\n\n```go\n// GetMap returns the registered map by name or absolute path.\nfunc GetMap(logger *slog.Logger, name string) *Map\n\n// GetOpenMaps returns API models of all currently open maps.\nfunc GetOpenMaps() []*models.BPFMap\n\n// GetModel returns the API model for a single map.\nfunc (m *Map) GetModel() *models.BPFMap\n```\n\n---\n\n## StateDB Reconciler Integration\n\nThe `NewMapOps` function bridges BPF maps with Cilium's StateDB reconciler:\n\n```go\nfunc NewMapOps[KV KeyValue](m *Map) reconciler.Operations[KV]\n```\n\nReturns a `reconciler.Operations` implementation backed by the BPF map. The reconciler will call `Update`, `Delete`, and `Prune` to keep the BPF map in sync with a StateDB table.\n\n**Error:** Returns `ErrMapNotOpened` if the map has not been opened before the reconciler starts.\n",

# Cilium eBPF Map API Reference

The `bpf` package provides Go wrappers for interacting with kernel eBPF maps from user space. It offers a high-level API for creating, reading, updating, and deleting map entries, as well as facilities for map pinning, event streaming, batch iteration, and eBPF collection loading.

---

## Table of Contents

1. [Key/Value Interfaces](#keyvalue-interfaces)
2. [Core Map Type and Creation](#core-map-type-and-creation)
3. [Map Lifecycle Operations](#map-lifecycle-operations)
4. [CRUD Operations](#crud-operations)
5. [Iteration and Dumping](#iteration-and-dumping)
6. [Batch Iterator](#batch-iterator)
7. [DumpStats](#dumpstats)
8. [Pinning and Persistence](#pinning-and-persistence)
9. [Event System](#event-system)
10. [Collection Loading](#collection-loading)
11. [EndpointKey (Concrete Key Example)](#endpointkey)
12. [Map Memory Flags](#map-memory-flags)

---

## Key/Value Interfaces

All map operations are typed through these interfaces. Any type used as a key or value in a `Map` must implement the corresponding interface.

### MapKey

```go
type MapKey interface {
    fmt.Stringer

    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapKey of the same
    // concrete type. Used internally to allocate buffers for iteration
    // and lookup.
    New() MapKey
}
```

### MapValue

```go
type MapValue interface {
    fmt.Stringer

    // New must return a pointer to a new, zero-value MapValue of the same
    // concrete type.
    New() MapValue
}
```

### MapPerCPUValue

For per-CPU map types (`PerCPUHash`, `PerCPUArray`, `LRUCPUHash`, `PerCPUCGroupStorage`), the value type must additionally implement `MapPerCPUValue`:

```go
type MapPerCPUValue interface {
    MapValue

    // NewSlice must return a pointer to a slice of structs implementing

... (truncated)
